The Mizan as the Universal Middle Term in Analogical Reasoning
Ibn Taymiyya expounds the mizan as the universal middle term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the universal common measure (mizan) in an analogical argument from usul al-fiqh and explain how it functions as the middle term.

Core Idea
The divine Mizan is the shared attribute that makes analogical reasoning just and certain.

Ibn Taymiyya connects the Quranic concept of al-Mizan (the Balance) to the logical tool of analogical reasoning. He argues that the Balance is not a literal scale but the universal common measure (al-wasf al-jami' al-mushtarak) that serves as the middle term in qiyas. This lesson unpacks how this insight grounds legal analogy in divine justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic verses and their interpretation of mizan
Ibn Taymiyya cites two verses (Ash-Shura 17 and Al-Hadid 25) that mention the Book and the Balance sent down with the messengers. He notes the Salaf interpreted mizan as justice or as a physical scale, but they are inseparable.
The key is that mizan is a divinely revealed tool for establishing justice.
2
Extract the logical function of mizan
Ibn Taymiyya defines mizan as that by which similarity and difference in attributes and quantities are known. It is a universal common measure (qadr mushtarak kulli) that exists between any two similar things.
Examples include physical balances for weight, measuring vessels for volume, sundials for time, and cubits for length.
3
See how this measure becomes the middle term in analogical reasoning
In legal and intellectual matters, the mizan is the comprehensive shared description (al-wasf al-jami' al-mushtarak) that connects the original (asl) and the branch (far'). This description is the 'illa (cause) and is called the middle term (al-hadd al-awsat).
Ibn Taymiyya redefines the Aristotelian middle term within the framework of Islamic legal analogy.
4
Analyze the wine/nabidh example to see the mizan in action
God forbade wine (khamr) because it distracts from prayer and causes enmity. Nabidh from grains shares this same intoxicating effect (the 'illa). The common attribute (intoxication) is the mizan that allows us to rule nabidh as similarly forbidden.
This is the classic qiyas that Ibn Taymiyya uses to illustrate the correct application of the mizan.
5
Understand the epistemological distinction between knowing universals vs weighing with both instances present
Ibn Taymiyya notes that knowing the universal without the particular is incomplete. The ideal weighing is when both the original and branch are present, similar to physically weighing two coins together. This prevents suspicion of bias and ensures justice.
He values concrete comparison over abstract reasoning alone, though both are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال سبحانه وتعالى: {الله الذي أنزل الكتاب بالحق والميزان} [سورة الشورى: 17]. وقال: {لقد أرسلنا رسلنا بالبينات وأنزلنا معهم الكتاب والميزان ليقوم الناس بالقسط} [سورة الحديد: 25]. و«الميزان» يفسره السلف بالعدل، ويفسره بعضهم بما يوزن به، وهما متلازمان. وقد أخبر أنه أنزل ذلك مع رسله كما أنزل معهم الكتاب ليقوم الناس بالقسط. فما يُعرف به تماثل المتماثلات من الصفات والمقادير هو من «الميزان»، وكذلك ما يُعرف به اختلاف المختلفات. فمعرفة أن هذه الدراهم أو غيرها من الأجسام الثقيلة بقدر هذه تعرف بموازينها. وكذلك معرفة أن هذا الكيل مثل هذا يعرف بميزانه، وهو المكاييل. وكذلك معرفة أن هذا الزمان مثل هذا الزمان يعرف بموازينه التي يقدر بها الأوقات، كما يُعرف به الظلال، وكما يجري من ماء ورمل وغير ذلك. وكذلك معرفة أن هذا بطول هذا يعرف بميزانه، وهو الذراع. فلا بد بين كل متماثلين من قدر مشترك كلي يعرف به أن أحدهما مثل الآخر. فكذلك الفروع المقيسة على أصولها في الشرعيات والعقليات تُعرف بالموازين المشتركة بينهما، وهي الوصف الجامع المشترك الذي يسمى الحد الأوسط. فإنا إذا علمنا أن الله حرم خمر العنب لما ذكره من أنها تصد عن ذكر الله وعن الصلاة وتوقع بين المؤمنين العداوة والبغضاء، ثم رأينا نبيذ الحبوب من الحنطة والشعير، والرز، وغير ذلك، يماثلها في المعنى الكلي المشترك الذي هو علة التحريم، كان هذا القدر المشترك الذي هو العلة هو الميزان التي أنزلها الله في قلوبنا لنزن بها هذا ونجعله مثل هذا، فلا نفرق بين المتماثلين. والقياس الصحيح هو من العدل الذي أمر الله تعالى به. ومن علم الكليات من غير معرفة المعين فمعه الميزان فقط، والمقصود بها وزن أحد الموزونين بالآخر. وإلا فالكليات لولا جزئياتها المعينات لم يكن بها اعتبار، كما أنه لولا الموزونات لم يكن إلى الميزان من حاجة. ولا ريب أنه إذا أحضر أحد الموزونين بالميزان واعتبر بالآخر بالميزان كان أتم في الوزن من أن يكون الميزان، وهو الوصف المشترك الكلي في العقل. أي شيء حضر من الأعيان المفردة وزن بها. فإن هذا أيضاً وزن صحيح؛ وذلك أحسن في الوزن. فإنك إذا وزنت بالصنجة قدراً من النقدين، ثم وزنت بها نظيره والأول شاهد والناس يشهدون أن هذا وزن به هذا فظهر مثله أو أكثر أو أقل، كان أحسن من أن يوزن أحدهما في مغيب الآخر. فإنه قد يُظن أن الوازن لم يعدل في الوزن كما يعدل إذا وزنهما معاً؛ فإن هذا يعتبر بأن يوزن أحدهما بالآخر بلا صنجة. وهكذا الموزونات بالعقل.
And He, the Most High, said: {Allah is the One who sent down the Book with truth and the Balance} [Surah Ash-Shura: 17]. And He said: {We have certainly sent Our messengers with clear proofs and sent down with them the Book and the Balance that mankind may maintain justice} [Surah Al-Hadid: 25]. The 'Balance' is interpreted by the Salaf as justice, and some interpret it as that with which one weighs, and they are inseparable. He informed that He sent that down with His messengers just as He sent down the Book with them so that people may maintain justice. So that by which the similarity of similar things in attributes and quantities is known is from 'the Balance', and likewise that by which the difference of different things is known. So the knowledge that these dirhams or other heavy bodies are equal to these is known by their balances. And likewise the knowledge that this measure is like this is known by its balance, which is the measuring vessels. And likewise the knowledge that this time is like this time is known by its balances by which times are estimated, as is known by shadows, and as from water and sand and other things. And likewise the knowledge that this is the length of this is known by its balance, which is the cubit. So between every two similar things there must be a universal common measure by which it is known that one is like the other. Likewise, the branches measured against their origins in legal and intellectual matters are known by the common balances between them, which is the comprehensive shared description called the middle term. For if we know that God forbade wine from grapes because of what He mentioned, that it distracts from the remembrance of God and from prayer and causes enmity and hatred among believers, then we see that nabidh from grains, wheat, barley, rice, and others, resembles it in the universal common meaning which is the cause of prohibition, then this common measure which is the cause is the balance that God sent down in our hearts so that we may weigh this with it and make it like this, and not differentiate between similar things. And the correct qiyas is from the justice that God, the Most High, commanded. And whoever knows universals without knowing the particular has only the balance with him, and the intended purpose of it is to weigh one of the two weighed things by the other. Otherwise, universals without their particular instances have no consideration, just as without the weighed things there would be no need for the balance. And there is no doubt that if one brings one of the two weighed things to the balance and considers it by the other with the balance, it is more complete in weighing than if the balance is the universal shared description in the mind. That is, if any individual thing is present, it is weighed by it. For this too is a correct weighing, and that is better in weighing. For if you weigh with the weight a quantity of coins, then weigh its like with it while the first is present and people witness that this was weighed by this and it appeared like, more, or less, that is better than weighing one in the absence of the other. For it may be suspected that the weigher did not balance as he would if he weighed them together; for this is considered by weighing one by the other without a weight. And likewise the weighed things by the intellect.
Source pages p. 416

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and epistemological expansion by Ibn Taymiyya on the concept of mizan (balance) as the universal middle term in correct analogical reasoning (qiyas). He begins by citing two Quranic verses that mention the 'Balance' (al-Mizan) sent down with the Book. He explains that the Salaf interpreted it as justice, and others as physical scales, but they are inseparable. The Balance is anything by which similarity and difference in attributes and quantities is known. He gives examples: weighing dirhams by balances, measuring volumes by measures, time by sundials, length by cubits. In all cases, there must be a universal common measure (qadr mushtarak kulli) to know similarity. Likewise, in legal and intellectual matters, branches are measured against origins by a shared description (wasf jam'i mushtarak) called the middle term (al-hadd al-awsat). He provides the example of wine (khamr) being forbidden due to its intoxicating effect (the cause 'illa), and then nabidh (date or grain drink) sharing that same cause, so it is also weighed by the same balance and ruled similar. He then explains that correct qiyas is an act of justice. He distinguishes between knowing universals without particulars (having only the balance) versus weighing with both examples present, which is more complete. He analogizes to physical weighing: weighing one coin against another while both are present is more reliable than weighing in absentia. Similarly, intellectual weighing is best when both the original and branch are present for comparison.

Key Terms
الميزان
الحد الأوسط
الوصف الجامع المشترك

Cause and Effect are Not Simultaneous
Ibn Taymiyya refutes the logical claim of temporal concomitance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's three-pronged refutation (Sharia, language, intellect) of the claim that cause and effect are concomitant in time, and apply it to a fiqh example of conditional divorce.

Core Idea
Cause and effect are not simultaneous: the effect always follows the cause.

The claim that cause and effect are concomitant in time (iqtirān al-‘illa wa al-ma‘lūl fī al-zamān) may seem plausible in abstract metaphysics, but Ibn Taymiyya shows it leads to serious errors in Islamic jurisprudence. In this passage, he dismantles the claim using three distinct lines of argument and illustrates the real-life consequence for conditional divorces. By mastering his refutation, you will learn to recognise when a metaphysical assumption conflicts with revealed law and linguistic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the logicians' claim
Locate in the Arabic where Ibn Taymiyya states the claim: that cause and effect can be concomitant in time. Note the examples they give: hand and ring, sun and rays, motion and sound.
The claim is not just metaphysical; it is used to justify erroneous fiqh rulings.
2
Extract the three refutation angles
Ibn Taymiyya explicitly lists three grounds: Sharia (شرعاً), language (لغة), and intellect (عقلاً). For each, find the key evidence: Sharia – the transmitted rulings from the Imams; Language – the meaning of fa (ف) and Quranic examples; Intellect – the impossibility of an agent being concomitant with its effect.
Each angle is independent and cumulatively decisive.
3
Apply to the fiqh example
Consider the conditional divorce: 'If I drink, then you are divorced.' According to the logicians' claim, the divorce would occur at the same moment as drinking. Ibn Taymiyya refutes this. Describe what he says about when the divorce actually occurs.
This shows the practical danger of a faulty metaphysical premise.

إبطال القول باقتران العلة والمعلول في الزمان

ولهذا من لم يُحكم معرفة هذا وإلا التبست عليه المعقولات ودخل عليه غلطهم - سواء كانوا قد غلطوا هم في التصور، وهو الغالب على أئمتهم؛ أو كانوا يقصدون التغليط، كما يفعله بعضهم . غلطهم جعل مثال ذلك : أنه إذا قيل لهم في مسئلة حدوث العالم: «كيف يكون العالم مفعولاً مصنوعاً للرب وهو مساوي له أزلاً وأبداً مقارن له في الزمان؟ هذا مما يعلم فساده بضرورة العقل، فإن المفعول لا يكون مقارناً للفاعل في الزمان» قالوا: بل هذا ممكن . وهو أن تقدم العلة على المعلول تقدماً عقلياً لازماً كتقدم حركة اليد على حركة الخاتم الذي فيها، وتقدم الشمس على الشُّعاع، وتقدم الحركة على الصوت الناشيء عنها» . ثم إن كان ممن تكلم في العلة والمعلول المذكور في الصفات والأحوال، وهو يقول العلم علة كون العالم عالماً كما يقوله مثبتوا الأحوال من النظار، كالقاضي أبي بكر، وأبي المعالي في أول قوليه والقاضي أبي يعلى وأمثالهم، فإنه قد ألف أن العلة والمعلول متلازمان مقترنان فلا يستنكر مثل هذا هنا . ولهذا غلط بسبب متابعتهم في هذا طوائفُ من الفقهاء في الفقه، كأبي المعالي وأتباعه أبي حامد والرافعي وغيرهم. فادَّعوا شيئاً خالفوا فيه جميع أئمة الفقه المتقدمين من أصحاب الأئمة الأربعة وغيرهم لم يقله الشافعي ولا أحد من أصحابه، ولا غيرهم. وهو أنه إذا قال لامرأته : إذا شربتُ أو زنيت، أو فعلت كذا، فأنت طالق ، وقصده أن يقع بها الطلاق إذا وجد ذلك الشرط ، أو قال: «إذا أعطيتني ألفاً فأنت طالق ، أو قال : إذا طلقتك فأنت طالق طلقة أخرى»، أو «إذا وقع عليك طلاقي فأنت طالق، أو قال مثل ذلك في العتق، فزعموا أن الحكم المعلق بشرط يقع هو والشرط معاً في زمن واحدٍ بناءً على أن الشرط علة للحكم، والمعلول يقارن العلة في الزمان .

وهذا خطأ شرعاً، ولغة وعقلاً. أما الشرع، فإن جميع الأحكام المعلقة بالشروط لا تقع منها شيء إلا عقيب الشروط، لا تقع مع الشروط والفروع المنقولة عن الأئمة تبين ذلك . وأما لغة، فإن الجزاء عند أهل اللغة يكون عقب الشرط وبعده، ولا يكون الجزاء مع الشرط في الزمان. ولهذا قد يكون الجزاء مما يتأخر زمانه، كقوله تعالى : فَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ خَيْرًا يَرَهُ وَمَن يَعْمَلْ مِثْقَالَ ذَرَّةٍ شَرًّا يَرَهُ ﴾ [سورة الزلزلة : ۷-۸] . وفي النذر إذا قال إن شفي الله مريضي فعلي صوم سنة فلا يجب عليه الصوم إلا بعد الشفاء، لا مقارناً للشفاء، ولا في زمن الشفاء. وكذلك إذا قال إن سَلّم الله مالي الغائب»، وكذلك إذا قال من رَدَّ عبدي الآبق» أو «بنى لي هذا الحائط ونحو ذلك . وأيضاً فهذا يذكر بحرف الفاء والفاء للتعقيب يوجب أن يكون الثاني عقيب الأول، لا معه. وأما عقلاً، فلأن الأول هنا كالفاعل الموجب للثاني . ولا يعرف قط أن الفاعل يقارنه مفعوله . وما ذكروه من اقتران العلة العقلية لمعلولها كـ «العلم» و «العالمية»، فجوابه أنه العلم هو العالمية وليس بسببها
Refuting the statement of the concomitance of cause and effect in time

Because of this, whoever does not have firm knowledge of this, otherwise intelligibles become confused for him and their error enters upon him—whether they themselves erred in conception, which is prevalent among their leaders, or they intended to mislead, as some of them do. Their error: they give as an example that when it is said to them in the issue of the temporal origination of the world: 'How can the world be an effect made by the Lord, while it is equal to Him in pre-eternity and post-eternity, concomitant with Him in time? This is known to be false by necessity of reason, for the effect cannot be concomitant with the cause in time,' they say: 'Rather, this is possible. And it is that the cause precedes the effect by a necessary intellectual precedence, like the precedence of the movement of the hand over the movement of the ring on it, and the precedence of the sun over the rays, and the precedence of the movement over the sound arising from it.' Then if he is among those who spoke about cause and effect mentioned in the attributes and states, and he says that knowledge is the cause of the world's being knowledgeable, as the affirmers of states among the theorists say, such as al-Qadi Abu Bakr, and Abu al-Ma'ali in his first position, and al-Qadi Abu Ya'la and their likes, then he is accustomed to the fact that cause and effect are necessarily concomitant and conjoined, so he does not find such [simultaneity] objectionable here. And because of this, groups of jurists in fiqh erred due to following them, such as Abu al-Ma'ali and his followers Abu Hamid and al-Rafi'i and others. They claimed something in which they contradicted all the leading jurists of the past among the followers of the four Imams and others; al-Shafi'i nor any of his companions nor others said it. And it is that if a man says to his wife: 'If I drink, or commit adultery, or do such-and-such, then you are divorced,' intending that divorce occur when that condition occurs, or he says: 'If you give me a thousand, then you are divorced,' or he says: 'If I divorce you, then you are divorced another divorce,' or 'If my divorce falls upon you, then you are divorced,' or he says something similar regarding emancipation, they claim that the ruling suspended on a condition occurs together with the condition in one time, based on the idea that the condition is a cause of the ruling, and the effect is concomitant with the cause in time.

And this is an error from the perspective of Sharia, language, and intellect. As for Sharia, indeed all rulings suspended on conditions do not occur except after the conditions; they do not occur with the conditions, and the transmitted branches from the Imams clarify that. As for language, indeed the consequence according to the people of language occurs after the condition and subsequent to it, and the consequence is not with the condition in time. Hence the consequence may be such that its time is delayed, like His statement: 'So whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it, and whoever does an atom's weight of evil will see it' [Surah al-Zalzala: 7-8]. And in a vow, if he says: 'If Allah heals my sick, then upon me is a year of fasting,' fasting is not obligatory upon him except after the healing, not concomitant with the healing, nor in the time of healing. Similarly if he says: 'If Allah returns my missing property,' and similarly if he says: 'Whoever returns my runaway slave' or 'builds this wall for me,' and the like. Also, this is mentioned with the letter fa, and fa indicates succession, requiring the second to be after the first, not with it. As for the intellect, because the first here is like the cause that necessitates the second. It is never known that a cause is concomitant with its effect. And what they mentioned about the intellectual cause being concomitant with its effect, like 'knowledge' and 'being knowledgeable,' the answer is that knowledge is the being knowledgeable and not because of it.
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation by Ibn Taymiyya of the logical claim that cause and effect are concomitant in time (اقتران العلة والمعلول في الزمان). He argues that this claim leads to errors in Islamic jurisprudence and is false from three perspectives: Sharia, language, and intellect.

Ibn Taymiyya begins by noting that those who lack firm knowledge of this issue fall into confusion and error. He then presents the example used by logicians: when asked about the creation of the world, they argue that it is possible for the effect to be concomitant with the cause in time, citing examples like the movement of the hand and the ring, the sun and its rays, and motion and sound. Some theologians who affirm states (ahwal), like al-Qadi Abu Bakr and Abu al-Ma'ali, further reinforce this by claiming that knowledge is the cause of the world's being knowledgeable, implying simultaneity.

Due to following these logicians, some later jurists (e.g., Abu al-Ma'ali, al-Ghazali, al-Rafi'i) made a grave error in fiqh. They claimed that in conditional divorces or expiations—such as a man saying to his wife, 'If I drink, then you are divorced'—the divorce occurs simultaneously with the condition. This contradicts the earlier consensus of the four Imams and their companions, including al-Shafi'i.

Ibn Taymiyya then refutes this from three angles:
- **From Sharia (شرعاً):** All rulings suspended on conditions occur after the condition, not with it. The established legal rulings from the Imams demonstrate this.
- **From Language (لغة):** In Arabic grammar, the consequence (جزاء) in conditional sentences occurs after the condition, not simultaneously. The letter 'fa' indicates succession. The Quranic verse 'Whoever does an atom's weight of good will see it' is an example: the seeing occurs after the deed, not with it. Similarly, vows and oaths take effect after the fulfillment of the condition.
- **From Reason (عقلاً):** The cause is like an agent that brings about the effect; we never observe an agent being concomitant with its effect. As for their example of knowledge and being knowledgeable, Ibn Taymiyya concludes that knowledge itself constitutes being knowledgeable; it is not a cause that is separate and simultaneous.

Key Terms
العلة
المعلول
اقتران
الشرط
الجزاء

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya demonstrates that the claim of temporal concomitance of cause and effect is false by Sharia, language, and reason; the effect always follows the cause, a principle essential for correct fiqh rulings.

Ibn Taymiyya's Reduction of Intuitive and Habitual to Experiential
Ibn Taymiyya reduces hadsiyyat and 'adiyyat to tajribiyat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that so-called intuitive (hadsiyyat) and habitual ('adiyyat) propositions are actually experiential reports, and explain why this undermines the claim to certain demonstration against an opponent.

Core Idea
What philosophers call 'intuitive' is just transmitted experience.

This lesson walks you through Ibn Taymiyya's radical critique: the philosophers' vaunted 'intuitive' (hadsiyyat) and 'habitual' ('adiyyat) premises are nothing more than experiential reports (tajribiyat). Once you see that, you realize that no true demonstration can be mounted against an opponent in these sciences, because the opponent can simply deny the underlying experience or report.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target principle
The philosophers claim that hadsiyyat (intuitive) and 'adiyyat (habitual) are certain premises that can ground demonstration. Find where Ibn Taymiyya states this in the passage.
He begins the fourth station: that these are from the category of tajribiyat.
2
Ibn Taymiyya's reduction
He asserts they fall under 'tajribiyat' (experiential). Notice how he argues that most people only know these through transmission (naql), not through immediate intuition.
This reduces certainty to the reliability of reports.
3
Examine the nature of experiential knowledge
He explains that experiential knowledge is not known by all; it is transmitted from some physicians or astronomers. What does this imply about its claim to be a foundation for demonstration?
If knowledge depends on transmission, an opponent may lack that transmission.
4
Test with a real example: astronomy
He uses astronomy to show that even the most rigorous philosophical science relies on sensory observation and individual reports, not mutawatir transmission.
Sensation only sees particular motions; the spheres are inferred.
5
Conclusion for demonstration
Since these premises are not certain, no burhan can be established against an opponent who denies them. The philosophers themselves admit this.
Burhan requires premises that are necessary and cannot be denied.

المقام الرابع - الوجه الثامن : كون الحدسيات والعاديات من باب التجربيات
«المجربات» إن كان علماً. فإن هذه لا يقوم فيها برهان على المنازع. فليس عند القوم برهان على المنازع. وأيضاً فإن كون هذه الأجسام الطبيعية جُرّبت، وكونَ الحركات الفلكية جربت لا يعرفه أكثر الناس إلا بالنقل والتواتر في هذا قليل. وإنما الغاية أن تنتقل التجربة في ذلك عن بعض الأطباء، أو بعض أهل الحساب.
وعلم الهيئة الذي هو أعظم علومهم الرياضية العقلية، الذي جَعَل أرسطو أهله هم تعرف أحكام أئمة الفلاسفة وعلمهم أصلَ ،الفلسفة فإنه منه تعرف عدد الأفلاك وحركاتها. وإلا علم الهيئة
فالحس لا يرى إلا حركة الأجسام المعينة، فيرى الشمس متحركة، والقمر متحركاً، والكواكب متحركة . هذا الذي يعلم بالحس. وأما كون هذه مركوزة (۱) في أفلاك متحركة فهذا إنما يعلمونه من علم الهيئة والعلم بأن بعض الأفلاك فوق بعض علموه بكسوف
·
الأسفل الأعلى، فلما رأوا القمر يكسف سائرها استدلوا بذلك على أنه تحت الجميع . ولما رأوا زُحَلَ لا يكسف شيئاً والجميع تكسفه استدلوا بذلك على أنه فوق / الجميع . وكذلك كون الثوابت في الثامن ادعوا علمه بأنها لا تكسف شيئاً بل قد يكسفها غيرها . وأما أفلاكها فاستدلوا عليها بالحركات .
والعلم بقدر حركاتها وبكسوف بعضها لبعض ونحو ذلك مداره على الأرصاد. العلم وغايته أن بعض الناس رأى هذا فأخبر به غيره وليس هذا خبراً متواتراً، بل مداره علی غالبه خبر واحد. ثم إن الأرصاد يقع فيها من الغلط ما هو معروف. ولهذا اختلفت الأرصاد
أرصاد المتقدمين والمتأخرين في حركة الثوابت - هل تقطع درجة فلكية في كل مئة سنة،
أو في ستة وستين وثلثي سنة كما زعمه أهلُ الرصد المأموني. ولما أخبرهم أهل الهيئة بحركة الفلك استدلوا بذلك على أن لها نَفْساً تحرّكه بالإرادة، لأن حركته دورية ليست العلم الإلهي طبيعية. واستدلوا على عدد النفوس التسعة بالأفلاك التسعة وعلى العقول العشرة بالأفلاك التسعة مع العقل العاشرة الذي هو أول صادر عن واجب الوجود». وجعلوا الفلك يتحرك للتشبه بالعلة الأولى ليخرج ما فيه من الأيون والأوضاع. وغاية الفلسفة التشبه بالعلة الأولى بحسب الإمكان. فهذا هو العلم الإلهي الذي هو عندهم الفلسفة الأولى والحكمة العليا. وفيه من المقدمات الضعيفة ما ليس هذا موضع بسطه . وإنما المقصود أن مبناه على قضايا يخبر بها بعض الناس عن قضايا حدسية. فإذا قالوا : إن هذه لا يقوم فيها برهان على المنازع، والقضايا الطبيعية مبناها على ما ينقله بعض الناس من التجارب، فإذا لم يكن في هذا ولا هذا برهان لم يكن عند القوم برهان على ما يختصون به. وأما ما يشتركون فيه هم وسائر الناس فهذا ليس مضافاً إليهم، ولا هو من علمهم . فأين البرهان على العلوم الفلسفية؟ مع العلم بأن العاديات التي هي علومهم الكلية منتقضة، كما بيناه في غير هذا الموضع . فنحن نعلم أنه ليس معهم في عامة ما يدعونه «برهانياً» برهان يقيني .
The fourth station - the eighth aspect: That the intuitive beliefs (hadsiyat) and habitual experiences ('adiyat) are from the category of experiential (tajribiyat). The experiential if it is knowledge: For these, no demonstration stands against the opponent. So the people (philosophers) have no demonstration against the opponent. Also, that these natural bodies have been experienced, and that the celestial movements have been experienced, most people do not know except through transmission and continuous transmission (tawatur) in this is little. Rather, the utmost is that experience in that is transmitted from some physicians or some astronomers. The science of astronomy, which is the greatest of their intellectual mathematical sciences, which Aristotle made its people know the judgments of the leading philosophers and their science the origin of philosophy, for from it the number of spheres and their movements are known. Sensation perceives only the motion of particular bodies, so it sees the sun moving, the moon moving, the stars moving. This is what is known by sensation. As for that these are embedded in moving spheres, that is only known from astronomy, and the knowledge that some spheres are above others they know by the eclipse of the lower by the higher. When they saw the moon eclipse all others, they inferred that it is beneath all. When they saw Saturn does not eclipse anything while all others eclipse it, they inferred that it is above all. Similarly, they claimed to know the fixed stars are in the eighth by that they do not eclipse anything but others eclipse them. As for their spheres, they inferred them from motions. Knowledge of the amount of their motions and their eclipses of each other and the like depends on observations, the utmost of which is that some people saw this and informed others, and this is not a mutawatir report; rather, its basis is mostly a single report. Then observations contain known errors. For this, the observations of the earlier and later astronomers differ regarding the motion of the fixed stars: whether they traverse a celestial degree every one hundred years or every sixty-six and two-thirds years as claimed by the observers of al-Ma'mun's time. When the astronomers informed them of the motion of the sphere, they inferred from that that it has a soul that moves it by will, because its motion is circular, not natural. They inferred the number of nine souls from the nine spheres, and the ten intellects from the nine spheres with the tenth intellect which is the first emanation from the Necessary Existent. They made the sphere move to imitate the First Cause in order to bring out what is in it of potentials and states. The utmost of philosophy is imitation of the First Cause as much as possible. This is the divine science which according to them is the first philosophy and the highest wisdom. It contains weak premises which this is not the place to elaborate. The point is that its foundation is upon propositions that some people report about intuitive propositions. So if they say: 'No demonstration stands in these against the opponent, and the natural propositions are based on what some people relate from experiences', then if there is no demonstration in this or that, then the people have no demonstration for what they specialize in. As for what they share with the rest of people, that is not attributed to them nor is it from their science. So where is the demonstration for the philosophical sciences? Even though the habitual sciences ('adiyat) which are their universal sciences are contradictory, as we have explained elsewhere. So we know that they do not have a certain demonstration in most of what they claim as 'demonstrative'.
Source pages p. 433

Commentary
This passage is part of Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' claim to possess demonstrative certainty (burhan) in their special sciences. He begins by stating the fourth station: that the so-called 'intuitive' and 'habitual' propositions fall under the category of 'experiential' knowledge. He argues that for experiential propositions, no demonstration can be mounted against an opponent who denies them, because they are not based on necessary premises but on sensory experience and reportage. He then examines the case of astronomy, which the philosophers consider their greatest intellectual science. He notes that most people only know celestial motions through transmission (naql) and that tawatur (mass transmission) is rare. The astronomers' knowledge of spheres, eclipses, and motions is based on observations ('arsad) which are often reported by individuals and subject to error, as shown by disagreements between earlier and later astronomers. Furthermore, from these uncertain observations, they infer speculative conclusions such as souls moving the spheres and a hierarchy of intellects, which form the basis of their 'divine science' (al-'ilm al-ilahi). This divine science is built on weak premises. The upshot is that if the philosophers themselves admit that no demonstration stands against an opponent in these matters, and if their natural science is based on transmitted experiments, then they have no demonstration for what is distinctive to their philosophy. Their only certain knowledge is what they share with all rational people, which is not unique to them. Hence, he asks rhetorically: 'Where is the demonstration for the philosophical sciences?' He adds that even the 'habitual sciences' ('adiyat), which are their universal principles, are often contradicted (muntaniqida). Therefore, we know that they lack certain demonstration in most of what they claim as demonstrative. This is a thorough critique of the epistemological foundations of Aristotelian science, characteristic of Ibn Taymiyya's radical skepticism toward Greek-based philosophy.

C) Because they are contradictory.
D) Because they are not known by the opponent.

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya reduces intuitive and habitual premises to experiential reports, showing that they cannot ground certain demonstration against an opponent.

Demonstration -- Burhan

Why Astronomers and Philosophers Lack Burhan According to Ibn Taymiyya
Ibn Taymiyya critiques astronomy and divine science.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to analyze Ibn Taymiyya's critique of the philosophers' divine science and astronomy as lacking certain demonstration due to reliance on fallible observations and weak inferences.

Core Idea
Astronomy and divine science are built on shaky observations and speculative inferences.

In this lesson, we follow Ibn Taymiyya's detailed deconstruction of astronomy ('ilm al-hay'a) and the divine science derived from it. He shows that their most celebrated science rests on observations prone to error and disagreement, and that their metaphysical conclusions (souls, intellects) are weak inferences. The result: no burhan here either.

Guided Path
1
Follow the astronomy example
Ibn Taymiyya takes astronomy as the philosophers' most rigorous science. What does he note about its foundations? He points out that knowledge of eclipses and motions depends on observations (arsad).
Observations are not mutawatir; they are reported by individuals.
2
Identify the sources of uncertainty
He lists: reliance on observations that are not mutawatir, disagreements among astronomers (e.g., precession rate), and the possibility of error. Find where he mentions these.
He explicitly says 'observations contain known errors' and cites the disagreement about the precession of fixed stars.
3
Trace the inferential chain
From observations of eclipses and motions, they infer the number of spheres, then souls moving the spheres, then intellects. Each step adds speculative elements. Map this chain from the passage.
The inference to souls and intellects is based on the circular motion of the sphere.
4
Evaluate the divine science
The pinnacle of philosophy (divine science) is built on these weak premises. Ibn Taymiyya says it contains 'weak premises'. What does this mean for its claim to be demonstrative?
If the premises are weak, the entire edifice lacks certainty.
5
Conclude: no burhan
Therefore, the philosophers have no certain demonstration for what is distinctive to their sciences. Summarize Ibn Taymiyya's final argument.
He asks rhetorically: 'So where is the demonstration for the philosophical sciences?'

Ibn Taymiyya's Critique of Demonstrative Proof in Philosophy
Ibn Taymiyya argues that philosophers lack certain demonstrative proof for their sciences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's argument that philosophers lack certain demonstrative proof for their sciences and evaluate its validity.

Core Idea
Philosophers claim certain proof, but their premises are conjectural and empirical, thus not demonstrative.

Ibn Taymiyya challenges the foundational claim of the philosophers that their sciences are built on certain demonstrative proofs (burhan). He argues that their premises are either based on conjectural reports or limited experiments, which cannot yield certainty. In this passage, he exposes the weakness of their epistemic foundation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target doctrine
What exactly are the philosophers claiming? They claim to have certain demonstrative proof (burhan) for their sciences, especially in philosophy and natural sciences.
This is the claim Ibn Taymiyya sets out to refute.
2
Locate Ibn Taymiyya's grounds
What type of objection does he make? He attacks the premises: they are based on conjectural reports (qadaya hadsiyya) from some people, and on empirical regularities ('adiyat) transmitted from experiments. Neither yields certainty.
He uses both epistemological and empirical grounds.
3
Analyze the reasoning
Ibn Taymiyya uses a conditional argument: if the premises are weak, then the proof cannot be certain. He also notes that what philosophers share with others is not their own, so it does not count for them.
The argument is a challenge to the universality of their claims.
4
Assess the conclusion
He concludes that the philosophers have no certain proof in what they claim, and that their universal sciences are contradictory. He will mention some contradictions as further evidence.
This is a strong refutation of the epistemic authority of philosophical sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ليس عندهم برهان على علومهم. وفيه من المقدمات الضعيفة ما ليس هذا موضع بسطه . وإنما المقصود أن مبناه على قضايا يخبر بها بعض الناس عن قضايا حدسية. فإذا قالوا : إن هذه لا يقوم فيها برهان على المنازع، والقضايا الطبيعية مبناها على ما ينقله بعض الناس من التجارب، فإذا لم يكن في هذا ولا هذا برهان لم يكن عند القوم برهان على ما يختصون به. وأما ما يشتركون فيه هم وسائر الناس فهذا ليس مضافاً إليهم، ولا هو من علمهم . فأين البرهان على العلوم الفلسفية؟ مع العلم بأن العاديات التي هي علومهم الكلية [۳۸۵] منتقضة، كما بيناه في غير هذا الموضع . فنحن نعلم أنه ليس معهم في عامة ما يدعونه «برهانياً» برهان يقيني . ولكن مع هذا نذكر بعض تناقضهم .
They do not have a proof for their sciences. It contains weak premises that this is not the place to expand. Rather, the point is that it is based on propositions that some people report about conjectural matters. If they say that these cannot be demonstrated against the opponent, and the natural sciences are based on what some people transmit from experiments, so if neither this nor that has a proof, then the people have no proof for what they specialize in. As for what they share with the rest of humanity, that is not attributed to them, nor is it part of their knowledge. So where is the proof for the philosophical sciences? Knowing that the regularities that are their universal sciences are contradictory, as we have shown elsewhere. So we know that they do not have, in most of what they claim to be 'demonstrative', a certain proof. But despite this, we mention some of their contradictions.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a critique. Ibn Taymiyya argues that the philosophers' sciences lack genuine demonstrative proof (burhan) because their premises are either based on conjectural reports (qadaya hadsiyya) or on experimental generalizations transmitted by some people. He notes that such premises cannot yield certainty, especially when the opponent disputes them. Moreover, the natural sciences rely on empirical regularities ('adiyat) that are not universally valid, as they can be contradicted. Thus, the philosophers' claim to have certain proof for their exclusive knowledge is false. What they share with others is not their own. Ibn Taymiyya concludes that he will mention some of their contradictions.

Why does Ibn Taymiyya deny that the philosophers have certain demonstrative proof (burhan) for their sciences?

C) Because they do not use syllogisms
D) Because they are atheists

Key Takeaway
Ibn Taymiyya's critique shows that demonstrative proof requires certain premises, which the philosophers fail to provide due to their reliance on conjectural and empirical sources.

The Inviolable Sunnah of Allah: Definition and Distinction
Ibn Taymiyya defines the inviolable sunnah of Allah and distinguishes its types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the witnessed and legislative sunnah as defined by Ibn Taymiyya using Qur'anic evidence.

Core Idea
Allah's sunnah is His consistent practice of supporting believers and punishing disbelievers, not the constancy of physical nature.

In this passage, Ibn Taymiyya defines the inviolable sunnah of Allah by citing Qur'anic verses that describe God's practice with past nations. He distinguishes between a sunnah that is observable in history and one that is known only by revelation, showing that the term 'sunnah' has a theological, not physical, meaning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Qur'anic verses quoted
List the three sets of verses (33:60-62, 48:22-23, 35:42-43) and note the common phrase 'lan tajida li-sunnat Allah tabdilan'.
2
Extract the definition
From the commentary, what exactly does Ibn Taymiyya say this sunnah consists of? (Support for believers, punishment for disbelievers.)
3
Note the distinction
Why does verse 33:38 lack the phrase 'lan tajida'? Because it refers to a legislative sunnah (shar'iyya) not seen by observation.
4
Contrast with natural regularity
Ibn Taymiyya explicitly contrasts this with physical customs like sunrise; the sunnah here is about outcomes of human actions.
5
Apply the definition
Check: would the support of believers always happen regardless of conditions? (No, it is conditional: 'if they fulfill their duty'.)

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنة الله التي لا تنتقض بحال ما أخبر الله أنها لا تنتقض، كقوله تعالى: {لَن لَّمْ يَنتَهِ الْمُتَنفِقُونَ وَالَّذِينَ فِي قُلُوبِهِم مَّرَضٌ وَالْمُرْجِفُونَ فِي الْمَدِينَةِ لَنُفْرِيَنَّكَ بِهِمْ ثُمَّ لَا يُجَاوِرُونَكَ فِيهَا إِلَّا قَلِيلًا مَّلْعُونِينَ أَيْنَمَا تُقِفُوا أَخِذُوا وَقُتِلُوا تَفْتِيلًا ) سُنَّةَ اللَّهِ فِي الَّذِينَ خَلَوْا مِن قَبْلُ وَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّةِ اللَّهِ تَبْدِيلًا ﴾ [سورة الأحزاب : ٦٠ - ٦٢]. وقال: {وَلَوْ قَتَلَكُمُ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا لَوَلَّوْا الْأَدْبَرَ ثُمَّ لَا يَجِدُونَ وَلِيًّا وَلَا نَصِيرًا لا سُنَّةَ اللَّهِ الَّتِي قَدْ خَلَتْ مِن قَبْلُ وَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّةِ اللَّهِ تَبْدِيلًا ﴾ [سورة الفتح : ۲۲ - ۲۳] وقال: ﴿ وَأَقْسَمُوا بِاللَّهِ جَهْدَ أَيْمَنِهِمْ لين جَاءَهُمْ نَذِيرٌ لَيَكُونُنَّ أَهْدَى مِنْ إِحْدَى الْأُمَمِ فَلَمَّا جَاءَهُمْ نَذِيرٌ مَا زَادَهُمْ إِلَّا نُفُورًا اسْتِكَبَارًا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَمَكَرَ الشَّي وَلَا يَحِيقُ الْمَكْرُ الشَّي إِلَّا بِأَهْلِهِ، فَهَلْ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَّا سُنَّتَ الْأَوَّلِينَ فَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللَّهِ تَبْدِيلًا وَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللَّهِ تَحْوِيلًا ﴾ [سورة فاطر : ٤٢ - ٤٣] . فهذه سنة الله وعادته في نصر عباده المؤمنين - إذا قاموا بالواجب ـ على الكافرين، نصر المؤمنين وانتقامه وعقوبته للكافرين الذين بلغتهم الرسلُ بعذاب من عنده أو بأيدي المؤمنين . هي سنة الله التي لا توجد منتقضة قط . ولما قال قبل هذا: ﴿ مَا كَانَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ مِنْ حَرَجٍ فِيمَا فَرَضَ اللَّهُ لَهُ سُنَّةَ اللهِ فِي الَّذِينَ خَلَوْا مِن قَبْلُ وَكَانَ أَمْرُ اللَّهِ قَدَرًا مَقدُورًا ﴾ [سورة الأحزاب : ٣٨]، لم يقل هنا ولن تجد لأن هذه سنة شرعية لا تُرى بالمشاهدة، بل تعلم بالوحي . بخلاف نصره للمؤمنين وعقوبته للمنذرين، فإنه أمر مشاهد [٣٨٦] فلن يوجد منتقضاً. وقد أراد بعض الملاحدة كالسُّهروردي المقتول في كتابه المبدأ والمعاد» الذي الاستدلال بهذه الآية سماه «الألواح العمادية» أن يجعل له دليلاً من القرآن والسنة على إلحاده. فاستدل على عدم تغير بهذه الآية على أن العالم لا يتغير، بل لا تزال الشمس تطلع وتغرب لأنها عادة الله . فيقال له : انخراق العادات أمر معلوم بالحس والمشاهدة بالجملة. وقد أخبر في غير موضع أن سبحانه لم يخلق العالم عبئاً وباطلاً، بل لأجل الجزاء. فكان هذا من سنته الجميلة، وهو جزاؤه الناسَ بأعمالهم في الدار الآخرة، كما أخبر به من نصر أوليائه وعقوبة أعدائه . فبَعْتُ الناس للجزاء هو من هذه السنة. وهو لم يخبر بأن كل عادة لا تنتقض ، بل أخبر عن السنة التي هي عواقب أفعال العباد بإثابة أولياءه ونصرهم على الأعداء . فهذه هي التي أخبر أنه لن يوجد لها تبديل ولا تحويل، كما قال: ﴿ فَهَلْ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَّا سُنَتَ الْأَوَّلِينَ فَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللهِ تَبْدِيلًا وَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللهِ تَحْوِيلًا ﴾ [سورة فاطر : ٤٣] . وذلك لأن العادة تتبع إرادة الفاعل، وإرادة الفاعل الحكيم هي إرادة حكيمة، إرادة الحكيم تقتضي التسوية فتسوي بين المتماثلات ولن يوجد لهذه السنة تبديل ولا تحويل، وهو إكرام أهل ولايته وطاعته ونصر رسله والذين آمنوا على المكذبين فهذه السنة تقتضيها حكمته سبحانه فلا انتقاض لها، بخلاف ما اقتضت حكمته تغييره. فذاك، تغييره من أيضاً من سنته التي لا يوجد لها تبديل ولا تحويل. لكن في هذه الآيات ردُّ على مَنْ يجعله يفعل [۳۸۷] بمجرد إرادة تُرجّح أحد المتماثلين بلا مُرجّح. فإن هؤلاء ليس عندهم له سنة لا تتبدل، ولا حكمة تقصد وهذا خلاف النصوص والعقول . فإن السنة تقتضي تماثل الآحاد وأن حكم الشيء حكم نظيره ، فيقتضي التسوية بين المتماثلات . وهذا خلاف قولهم .
The sunnah of Allah that is never violated in any case is what Allah has informed that it is not violated, such as His saying: {If the hypocrites and those in whose hearts is disease and those who spread false news in the city do not cease, We will surely incite you against them; then they will not be your neighbors in it except for a little, accursed wherever they are found, they will be seized and killed with a (violent) killing. (That is) the sunnah of Allah with those who passed away before, and you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any change} [33:60-62]. And He said: {And if those who disbelieve fight you, they will turn their backs, then they will not find a protector or a helper. (That is) the sunnah of Allah which has occurred before, and you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any change} [48:22-23]. And He said: {And they swore by Allah their strongest oaths that if a warner came to them, they would be more guided than any one of the nations; but when a warner came to them, it only increased them in aversion, (due to) arrogance in the land and plotting of evil; but the evil plot does not encompass except its own people. Then do they await except the sunnah of the former ones? And you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any change, and you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any alteration} [35:42-43]. So this is Allah's sunnah and His custom in supporting His believing servants—when they fulfill their duty—over the disbelievers: supporting the believers and His revenge and punishment for the disbelievers who were reached by the messengers, with punishment from Him or by the hands of the believers. It is Allah's sunnah that is never found violated. And when He said before this: {There is no blame on the Prophet in what Allah has made permissible for him. That is Allah's sunnah with those who passed away before. And the command of Allah is a determined decree} [33:38], He did not say here 'and you will not find' because this is a legislative sunnah that is not seen by observation, but is known by revelation. Unlike His support for the believers and punishment of the warners, for it is a witnessed matter, so it will not be found violated. And some atheists like al-Suhrawardi al-Maqtul in his book 'al-Mabda' wa al-Ma'ad' which he called 'al-Alwah al-Imadiyya' wanted to make this verse a proof for his atheism. So he used it to argue that the world does not change, rather the sun rises and sets because it is Allah's custom. So it is said to him: The breaking of customs is known by sense and observation in general. And He has informed in more than one place that He did not create the world in vain and falsehood, but for recompense. So this is part of His beautiful sunnah, and it is His recompensing people for their deeds in the Hereafter, as He informed of supporting His friends and punishing His enemies. So sending people for recompense is part of this sunnah. And He did not inform that every custom is not violated, but He informed about the sunnah which is the consequences of the actions of servants, rewarding His friends and supporting them against the enemies. This is what He informed that there will be no substitution or alteration for it. And that is because custom follows the will of the agent, and the will of the wise agent is a wise will. The will of the wise necessitates equality, so it makes equal between similar things, and there will be no substitution or alteration for this sunnah, and it is honoring the people of His loyalty and obedience and supporting His messengers and those who believe against the deniers. So this sunnah is necessitated by His wisdom, so it has no violation, unlike what His wisdom necessitated its change. So that, its change is also part of His sunnah that has no substitution or alteration. However, in these verses is a refutation of those who make Him act by mere will that prefer one of two similars without a preferred. For these people have no unchangeable sunnah for Him, no wisdom intended. This contradicts the texts and intellects. For the sunnah necessitates the similarity of individuals and that the ruling of a thing is the ruling of its equivalent, so it necessitates equality between similars. This is contrary to their statement.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition of the concept of the inviolable sunnah of Allah. Ibn Taymiyya begins by quoting Qur'anic verses that mention sunnat Allah, showing that it refers to His practice of supporting believers and punishing disbelievers. He distinguishes between a legislative sunnah (like permissibility) that is known by revelation and a witnessed sunnah (like historical punishments) that is observable. He then refutes the misinterpretation by al-Suhrawardi, who argued that the constancy of natural phenomena (like the rising of the sun) is an unchangeable sunnah, implying the world is eternal and unchanged. Ibn Taymiyya responds that the breaking of customs (miracles) is known by observation, and the verses refer to the sunnah of recompense, not physical constancy. He further explains that the sunnah of Allah is based on His wisdom, which requires equality between similar things. This refutes the occasionalist view that God acts arbitrarily without cause. The passage concludes that the sunnah implies consistent rulings for similar cases, opposing those who deny divine wisdom.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, why is the phrase 'lan tajida' not found in Q. 33:38?
A) Because the verse was abrogated
B) Because it refers to a legislative sunnah not seen by observation
C) Because the Prophet's marriage was unique
D) Because the verse is about a past sunnah that is no longer valid

Key Takeaway
Sunnat Allah in these verses is a theological principle of divine justice, not a physical law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: In Q. 48:23, Allah says 'sunnat Allah allati qad khalat min qablu.' Based on the context of the verse, determine whether this sunnah belongs to the witnessed or legislative type. Justify your answer using Ibn Taymiyya's criteria.
?

Refuting Suhrawardi's Misuse of the Sunnah Verses
Ibn Taymiyya refutes Suhrawardi's misuse of sunnah verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Suhrawardi's misinterpretation and reconstruct Ibn Taymiyya's refutation using the distinction between sunnah of recompense and physical custom.

Core Idea
Suhrawardi twisted the verses to argue for an unchanging world, but Ibn Taymiyya shows they refer to divine recompense, not physical constant.

Ibn Taymiyya directly refutes al-Suhrawardi's attempt to use the sunnah verses to support the idea of an unchanging world. He points out that miracles (kharaq al-'ada) are known by sense, and the verses speak of God's sunnah in rewarding and punishing, not the constancy of natural phenomena. Moreover, God's wisdom necessitates equality between similar cases, undermining the occasionalist notion of arbitrary divine will.

Guided Path
1
State Suhrawardi's argument
He used Q. 33:62 to argue that the world does not change, e.g., the sun always rises and sets because it is Allah's custom.
2
Identify Ibn Taymiyya's first response
The breaking of customs (miracles) is known by sense and observation, so not all customs are unchangeable.
3
Identify the second response
The verses refer to the sunnah of recompense (jaza'), not to physical regularity. The world was created for recompense.
4
Understand the role of divine wisdom
God's wisdom necessitates consistency in reward and punishment, so the sunnah is about that, not about arbitrary will. Wisdom requires equality between similar cases.
5
Assess the refutation
Conclude that Suhrawardi's misuse stems from ignoring the context and the distinction between types of sunnah.

جَاءَهُمْ نَذِيرٌ مَا زَادَهُمْ إِلَّا نُفُورًا اسْتِكَبَارًا فِي الْأَرْضِ وَمَكَرَ الشَّي وَلَا يَحِيقُ الْمَكْرُ الشَّي إِلَّا بِأَهْلِهِ، فَهَلْ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَّا سُنَّتَ الْأَوَّلِينَ فَلَن وقد أخبر في غير موضع أن سبحانه لم يخلق العالم عبئاً وباطلاً، بل لأجل الجزاء. فكان هذا من سنته الجميلة، وهو جزاؤه الناسَ بأعمالهم في الدار الآخرة، كما أخبر به من نصر أوليائه وعقوبة أعدائه . فبَعْتُ قال: ﴿ فَهَلْ يَنظُرُونَ إِلَّا سُنَتَ الْأَوَّلِينَ فَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللهِ تَبْدِيلًا وَلَن تَجِدَ لِسُنَّتِ اللهِ تَحْوِيلًا ﴾ [سورة فاطر : ٤٣] . وذلك لأن العادة تتبع إرادة الفاعل، وإرادة المتماثلين بلا مُرجّح. فإن هؤلاء ليس عندهم له سنة لا تتبدل، ولا حكمة تقصد وهذا خلاف النصوص والعقول . فإن السنة تقتضي تماثل الآحاد وأن حكم الشيء حكم نظيره ، فيقتضي التسوية بين المتماثلات . وهذا خلاف قولهم .
The sunnah of Allah that is never violated in any case is what Allah has informed that it is not violated, such as His saying: {If the hypocrites and those in whose hearts is disease and those who spread false news in the city do not cease, We will surely incite you against them; then they will not be your neighbors in it except for a little, accursed wherever they are found, they will be seized and killed with a (violent) killing. (That is) the sunnah of Allah with those who passed away before, and you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any change} [33:60-62]. And He said: {And if those who disbelieve fight you, they will turn their backs, then they will not find a protector or a helper. (That is) the sunnah of Allah which has occurred before, and you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any change} [48:22-23]. And He said: {And they swore by Allah their strongest oaths that if a warner came to them, they would be more guided than any one of the nations; but when a warner came to them, it only increased them in aversion, (due to) arrogance in the land and plotting of evil; but the evil plot does not encompass except its own people. Then do they await except the sunnah of the former ones? And you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any change, and you will not find for the sunnah of Allah any alteration} [35:42-43]. So this is Allah's sunnah and His custom in supporting His believing servants—when they fulfill their duty—over the disbelievers: supporting the believers and His revenge and punishment for the disbelievers who were reached by the messengers, with punishment from Him or by the hands of the believers. It is Allah's sunnah that is never found violated. And when He said before this: {There is no blame on the Prophet in what Allah has made permissible for him. That is Allah's sunnah with those who passed away before. And the command of Allah is a determined decree} [33:38], He did not say here 'and you will not find' because this is a legislative sunnah that is not seen by observation, but is known by revelation. Unlike His support for the believers and punishment of the warners, for it is a witnessed matter, so it will not be found violated. And some atheists like al-Suhrawardi al-Maqtul in his book 'al-Mabda' wa al-Ma'ad' which he called 'al-Alwah al-Imadiyya' wanted to make this verse a proof for his atheism. So he used it to argue that the world does not change, rather the sun rises and sets because it is Allah's custom. So it is said to him: The breaking of customs is known by sense and observation in general. And He has informed in more than one place that He did not create the world in vain and falsehood, but for recompense. So this is part of His beautiful sunnah, and it is His recompensing people for their deeds in the Hereafter, as He informed of supporting His friends and punishing His enemies. So sending people for recompense is part of this sunnah. And He did not inform that every custom is not violated, but He informed about the sunnah which is the consequences of the actions of servants, rewarding His friends and supporting them against the enemies. This is what He informed that there will be no substitution or alteration for it. And that is because custom follows the will of the agent, and the will of the wise agent is a wise will. The will of the wise necessitates equality, so it makes equal between similar things, and there will be no substitution or alteration for this sunnah, and it is honoring the people of His loyalty and obedience and supporting His messengers and those who believe against the deniers. So this sunnah is necessitated by His wisdom, so it has no violation, unlike what His wisdom necessitated its change. So that, its change is also part of His sunnah that has no substitution or alteration. However, in these verses is a refutation of those who make Him act by mere will that prefer one of two similars without a preferred. For these people have no unchangeable sunnah for Him, no wisdom intended. This contradicts the texts and intellects. For the sunnah necessitates the similarity of individuals and that the ruling of a thing is the ruling of its equivalent, so it necessitates equality between similars. This is contrary to their statement.
Source pages p. 434

Commentary
This passage is a critical exposition of the concept of the inviolable sunnah of Allah. Ibn Taymiyya begins by quoting Qur'anic verses that mention sunnat Allah, showing that it refers to His practice of supporting believers and punishing disbelievers. He distinguishes between a legislative sunnah (like permissibility) that is known by revelation and a witnessed sunnah (like historical punishments) that is observable. He then refutes the misinterpretation by al-Suhrawardi, who argued that the constancy of natural phenomena (like the rising of the sun) is an unchangeable sunnah, implying the world is eternal and unchanged. Ibn Taymiyya responds that the breaking of customs (miracles) is known by observation, and the verses refer to the sunnah of recompense, not physical constancy. He further explains that the sunnah of Allah is based on His wisdom, which requires equality between similar things. This refutes the occasionalist view that God acts arbitrarily without cause. The passage concludes that the sunnah implies consistent rulings for similar cases, opposing those who deny divine wisdom.

Checkpoint
According to Ibn Taymiyya, what is the main flaw in Suhrawardi's argument?
A) He uses a weak hadith
B) He confuses the sunnah of recompense with physical custom
C) He denies the existence of God
D) He relies on an invalid syllogism

Key Takeaway
Suhrawardi's error lies in ignoring the context and purpose of the verses; they speak of divine justice, not physics.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Task 1: Suhrawardi claimed that 'sunnat Allah' in the verses proves that the sun's rising is an unchangeable custom. Write a brief rebuttal using Ibn Taymiyya's distinction between the sunnah of recompense and physical customs.
?
Task 2: In the passage, Ibn Taymiyya says that the sunnah necessitates similarity between similar things. Explain how this principle refutes the occasionalist view that God acts by mere will without wisdom.
